Bottom-Up Refactoring Strategy

Start Here
üéØ The Foundation-First Approach
Build from the ground up, one layer at a time. Each layer must be solid before building the next. Like a skyscraper: you don't add floors before the concrete sets.

Rule: Never move to the next layer until current layer health checks pass.
üèõÔ∏è zCLI Architecture Layers
Layer 0: Foundation (Weeks 1-2)
zConfig, zComm, zServer ‚Üí Makes everything else possible
Layer 1: Core Services (Weeks 3-5)
zAuth, zDisplay, zParser, zLoader, zDialog ‚Üí Daily tools
Layer 2: Business Logic (Weeks 6-9)
zData, zShell, zWizard, zUtils ‚Üí Heavy lifters
Layer 3: Orchestration (Week 10)
zWalker, zNavigation ‚Üí Conductor
üèóÔ∏è Layer 0: Foundation (Weeks 1-2)
Goal: 9.5/10 Stability
Why First: If foundation cracks later, everything above collapses. These subsystems are used by ALL others.
Success Criteria: Zero breaking changes possible, 100% test coverage, complete documentation.

üéØ Testing Strategy: Use REAL tests for async/network subsystems (zBifrost, zServer), not just mocks.
Reason: Mocks can't catch port conflicts, network timeouts, or race conditions - and zBifrost is the killer feature.

Week 3.2: üîê Persistent sessions (Authentication State) ‚úÖ COMPLETE
Goal: "Remember me" functionality - login once, stay authenticated for 7 days (survives app restarts)
Note: This is NOT wizard batching (that's zShell canvas mode). This is about user login persistence.

‚úÖ IMPLEMENTED (The zCLI Way - Declarative):
  1. ‚úÖ Created zSchema.sessions.yaml (declarative table definition)
  2. ‚úÖ Uses z.data.insert/select/update/delete for all operations (no raw SQL!)
  3. ‚úÖ Auto-cleanup expired sessions via zData
  4. ‚úÖ CREATE TABLE before INSERT (critical: DDL before DML!)

üóÇÔ∏è Schema (zSchema.sessions.yaml):
  ‚Ä¢ Meta: Data_Type: sqlite, Data_Path: "zMachine" (platformdirs)
  ‚Ä¢ Fields: session_id (pk), user_id, username, password_hash, token, created_at, expires_at, last_accessed

üîß Implementation:
  ‚Ä¢ z.auth._ensure_sessions_db() - Load schema + CREATE TABLE if not exists
  ‚Ä¢ z.auth._load_session() - Restore valid session on startup
  ‚Ä¢ z.auth._save_session() - Persist login state (bcrypt hash)
  ‚Ä¢ z.auth._cleanup_expired() - Remove old sessions
  ‚Ä¢ z.auth.login(persist=True) - Save to sessions.db
  ‚Ä¢ z.auth.logout() - Delete persistent session

üìÅ Cross-Platform Paths (via platformdirs):
  ‚Ä¢ macOS: ~/Library/Application Support/zolo-zcli/sessions.db
  ‚Ä¢ Linux: ~/.local/share/zolo-zcli/sessions.db
  ‚Ä¢ Windows: %LOCALAPPDATA%\zolo-zcli\sessions.db

‚úÖ Tests Added: 10 comprehensive unit tests in zAuth_Test.py
  ‚Ä¢ test_ensure_sessions_db_success - Schema + table creation
  ‚Ä¢ test_save_session_creates_record - Correct fields
  ‚Ä¢ test_save_session_generates_unique_tokens - Token uniqueness
  ‚Ä¢ test_load_session_restores_valid_session - Restore on startup
  ‚Ä¢ test_load_session_ignores_expired_session - Expiry check
  ‚Ä¢ test_cleanup_expired_removes_old_sessions - Housekeeping
  ‚Ä¢ test_logout_deletes_persistent_session - Cleanup
  ‚Ä¢ test_login_with_persist_saves_session - persist=True
  ‚Ä¢ test_login_with_persist_false_skips_save - persist=False
  ‚Ä¢ test_session_duration_is_7_days - Expiry calculation

üí° Critical Learning: zData separates DDL (CREATE/DROP) from DML (INSERT/SELECT/UPDATE/DELETE). Loading a schema does NOT auto-create tables - you must explicitly call z.data.create_table() before INSERT operations!

‚úÖ Total Tests: 931 passing (was 921, +10 from Week 3.2) üéâ

Layer 1 zAuth zData 2 days ‚úÖ DONE
Week 3.3: üîê Enhanced RBAC with Inline `_rbac` Directives (Declarative) ‚úÖ COMPLETE
Goal: Flask-Login style RBAC using inline YAML directives (no Python decorators!)
Design: Declarative access control with default public access (opt-in security)

‚úÖ IMPLEMENTED (Final Syntax - Inline `_rbac`):
  ‚Ä¢ Default: Public access (no restrictions unless `_rbac` specified)
  ‚Ä¢ Inline `_rbac` key within each zUI item's dictionary
  ‚Ä¢ Auth Implied: `require_role`/`require_permission` auto-require authentication

üìã Final Syntax (Inline `_rbac` - NOT `!` Prefix):
# Public access (default - no _rbac)
"^Login":
  zDisplay: ...

# Authentication only
"^Dashboard":
  _rbac:
    require_auth: true
  zDisplay: ...

# Role required (auth implied)
"^Edit Settings":
  _rbac:
    require_role: "user"
  zDisplay: ...

# Multiple roles OR logic (auth implied)
"^Moderate":
  _rbac:
    require_role: ["admin", "moderator"]
  zDisplay: ...

# Role + Permission AND logic (auth implied)
"^Delete Data":
  _rbac:
    require_role: "admin"
    require_permission: "data.delete"
  zDisplay: ...

üîß Implementation (‚úÖ COMPLETE):
  1. ‚úÖ Extended zSchema.sessions.yaml - Added role field (default: "user")
  2. ‚úÖ Created zSchema.permissions.yaml - User permissions table (id, user_id, permission, granted_by, granted_at)
  3. ‚úÖ Added to zAuth:
      ‚Ä¢ has_role(role) - Check user role (supports single/list)
      ‚Ä¢ has_permission(permission) - Check user permission
      ‚Ä¢ grant_permission(user_id, permission, granted_by) - Admin-only
      ‚Ä¢ revoke_permission(user_id, permission) - Admin-only
  4. ‚úÖ Updated zParser - Parse inline _rbac directives from zUI items
  5. ‚úÖ Updated zLoader - Pass session context to parser for RBAC processing
  6. ‚úÖ Updated zWizard - Enforce RBAC before executing zKey (_check_rbac_access)
  7. ‚úÖ Clear "Access Denied" messages (Terminal + zBifrost compatible, no blocking)

üìã RBAC Features (All Implemented):
  ‚Ä¢ ‚úÖ require_auth: true - Authentication required (any role)
  ‚Ä¢ ‚úÖ require_role: "admin" - Single role (auth implied)
  ‚Ä¢ ‚úÖ require_role: ["admin", "moderator"] - Multiple roles, OR logic (auth implied)
  ‚Ä¢ ‚úÖ require_permission: "data.delete" - Permission check (auth implied)
  ‚Ä¢ ‚úÖ Combined directives (AND logic): role + permission both required
  ‚Ä¢ ‚úÖ Public access default - No `_rbac` = no restrictions (opt-in security)

‚úÖ Tests Added (18 comprehensive tests - 100% pass rate):
  ‚Ä¢ TestRBACParsing (6 tests) - Inline `_rbac` extraction, public default
  ‚Ä¢ TestRBACEnforcement (11 tests) - Access control logic, auth/role/permission checks
  ‚Ä¢ TestRBACIntegration (1 test) - RBAC with zData operations
  ‚Ä¢ TestRBACEdgeCases (2 tests) - Error handling, safety fallbacks
  ‚Ä¢ File: zTestSuite/zRBAC_Test.py
  ‚Ä¢ Integrated: zTestSuite/run_all_tests.py

üéØ Key Design Decisions:
  ‚Ä¢ Inline > Prefix: Switched from `!require_*` prefix to inline `_rbac` key (solved YAML duplicate key issue)
  ‚Ä¢ Public by Default: No `_rbac` = public access (opt-in security, reduces boilerplate)
  ‚Ä¢ Auth Implied: `require_role`/`require_permission` auto-require authentication (simplified YAML)
  ‚Ä¢ No Conflict: `_rbac` inline key doesn't conflict with existing `!` suffix modifier (required step retry logic)
  ‚Ä¢ UX First: Clear access denied messages with reasons, sandbox-compatible (no blocking input prompts)

üìä Benefits Achieved:
  ‚úÖ Declarative (RBAC rules in YAML, not Python)
  ‚úÖ Item-level scoping (precise control)
  ‚úÖ Flask-Login style (familiar pattern)
  ‚úÖ Cross-platform (Terminal + zBifrost)
  ‚úÖ AI-friendly (clean inline syntax)
  ‚úÖ Clean syntax (no YAML quoting issues)

  ‚Ä¢ Modified: zWizard.py (enforcement), AGENT.md (patterns + pitfalls)

Week 5.2: üìù zDialog Auto-Validation (Close the Critical Gap!) üéØ
üéØ GOAL: Auto-wire zDialog forms to zSchema validation rules for real-time validation feedback (COMPLETE!)

‚ùå CURRENT STATE (The Critical Gap):
  ‚Ä¢ User fills form ‚Üí submits ‚Üí server validates ‚Üí error returned
  ‚Ä¢ Problem: Wasted round-trip, poor UX, invalid data reaches server
  ‚Ä¢ Workaround: Manual validation via z.data.insert() (server-side only)

‚úÖ DESIRED STATE (After Week 5.2):
  ‚Ä¢ User fills form ‚Üí real-time validation ‚Üí errors shown before submit
  ‚Ä¢ Solution: zDialog reads model: '@.zSchema.users' ‚Üí auto-applies all validation rules
  ‚Ä¢ Benefit: No wasted round-trip, immediate feedback, consistent validation

üìã Implementation Tasks (5 steps):

1. ‚úÖ Read model attribute from zUI (zParser integration)
  ‚Ä¢ Detect model: '@.zSchema.users' in zDialog block
  ‚Ä¢ Pass model reference to zDialog handler
  ‚Ä¢ Handle missing/invalid model gracefully (skip auto-validation)

2. ‚úÖ Load zSchema and extract validation rules (zLoader integration)
  ‚Ä¢ Use z.loader.handle(model_path) to load schema
  ‚Ä¢ Extract validation rules for each field in the form
  ‚Ä¢ Map field names to rules: {field_name: {required, min, max, pattern, format, error_message}}

3. ‚úÖ Apply validation before form submission (DataValidator integration)
  ‚Ä¢ Call DataValidator.validate_field() for each form field
  ‚Ä¢ Collect all validation errors (don't stop at first failure)
  ‚Ä¢ Return validation errors before attempting INSERT/UPDATE

4. ‚úÖ Display field-specific errors (zDisplay integration)
  ‚Ä¢ Terminal Mode: Show errors inline with field names (existing ValidationError format)
  ‚Ä¢ zBifrost Mode: Emit WebSocket event with field errors (JSON format for client-side display)
  ‚Ä¢ Use Week 4.3 ValidationError for actionable hints (üí° format)

5. ‚úÖ Comprehensive tests (Terminal + zBifrost modes)
  ‚Ä¢ Test auto-validation with valid/invalid data
  ‚Ä¢ Test missing model (graceful fallback to manual validation)
  ‚Ä¢ Test all validation types (required, pattern, format, min/max, length)
  ‚Ä¢ Test error display in both modes

üéØ Example Usage (After Week 5.2):
# In zUI.users.yaml
"^Add User":
  zDialog:

    fields:
      - username # Will auto-validate against pattern: "^[a-zA-Z0-9_]{3,20}$"
      - email # Will auto-validate against format: email
      - age # Will auto-validate against min: 18, max: 120
  zData:
    action: insert
    table: users

Week 5.4: üìù Add Plugin Validators (Extension Point - AUGMENT, NOT REPLACE) ‚úÖ COMPLETE
üéØ GOAL: Extend built-in validation with domain-specific custom validators using zCLI's native plugin pattern

üîë CORE DESIGN PHILOSOPHY:
  ‚Ä¢ AUGMENT, NOT REPLACE: Plugin validators run AFTER built-in validators (layered validation)
  ‚Ä¢ Consistent Syntax: Use same &PluginName.function(args) pattern as zFunc, zDispatch
  ‚Ä¢ Fail-Fast: Built-in validators run first (structural), plugin validators second (business logic)
  ‚Ä¢ Separation of Concerns: Built-in = structure/format, Plugin = business rules
  ‚Ä¢ NO OVERRIDE: Both validators run (if built-in fails, plugin never executes)

üìã Implementation Tasks (5 steps):

1. ‚úÖ Pass zcli to DataValidator initialization
  ‚Ä¢ Modify zData operations: validator = DataValidator(schema, logger, zcli)
  ‚Ä¢ Store zcli instance in DataValidator for plugin resolution
  ‚Ä¢ Maintain backward compatibility (zcli=None default)

2. ‚úÖ Add _check_plugin_validator() method to DataValidator
  ‚Ä¢ Detect validator: "&validators.check_email_domain(['company.com'])" in rules
  ‚Ä¢ Use self.zcli.zparser.resolve_plugin_invocation() (reuse existing infrastructure!)
  ‚Ä¢ Inject validator-specific arguments: user_args + [value, field_name] + {table, full_data}
  ‚Ä¢ Handle graceful degradation if plugin not found (log warning, skip validation)

3. ‚úÖ Update _validate_field() execution order
  ‚Ä¢ Layer 1: Built-in string rules (min_length, max_length)
  ‚Ä¢ Layer 2: Built-in numeric rules (min, max)
  ‚Ä¢ Layer 3: Built-in pattern rules (regex)
  ‚Ä¢ Layer 4: Built-in format rules (email, url, phone)
  ‚Ä¢ Layer 5 (NEW): Plugin validator (if specified) ‚Üê ONLY runs if all above pass!
  ‚Ä¢ Return error at first failure (fail-fast principle)

4. ‚úÖ Define validator plugin contract
  ‚Ä¢ Signature: def validator_name(user_args, value, field_name, **kwargs)
  ‚Ä¢ Return: (is_valid: bool, error_msg: str or None)
  ‚Ä¢ Kwargs Context: {table: str, full_data: dict} for cross-field validation
  ‚Ä¢ User Args: From schema (e.g., ['company.com', 'partner.com'])

5. ‚úÖ Create comprehensive tests + demo
  ‚Ä¢ Plugin validator loading (cache integration)
  ‚Ä¢ Chaining (built-in pass ‚Üí plugin runs, built-in fail ‚Üí plugin skipped)
  ‚Ä¢ Error handling (plugin not found, plugin exception)
  ‚Ä¢ Integration with Week 5.2 auto-validation (zDialog forms)
  ‚Ä¢ Example validators: check_email_domain, check_username_blacklist, check_sku_uniqueness

üéØ Example Usage (Declarative YAML):
# In zSchema.users.yaml
email:
  type: str
  required: true
  rules:
    format: email # ‚úÖ Layer 1: Built-in validator (structural)
    validator: "&validators.check_email_domain(['company.com', 'partner.com'])" # ‚úÖ Layer 2: Plugin validator (business logic)
    error_message: "Email must be from company.com or partner.com"

# Example with plugin-only validation (no built-in)
department:
  type: str
  rules:
    validator: "&validators.check_department_active()" # Only plugin runs

üîß Validator Plugin Contract (plugins/validators.py):
# User args come first, then injected args
def check_email_domain(allowed_domains, value, field_name, **kwargs):
  """Validate email domain against allowed list.
  
  Args:
    allowed_domains (list): User-provided from schema
    value (str): Field value (auto-injected)
    field_name (str): Field name (auto-injected)
    **kwargs: Context (table, full_data)
  
  Returns:
    tuple: (is_valid: bool, error_msg: str or None)
  """
  if '@' not in value:
    return False, f"{field_name} must be a valid email"
  
  domain = value.split('@')[1]
  if domain not in allowed_domains:
    return False, f"{field_name} must use approved domain: {', '.join(allowed_domains)}"
  
  return True, None # ‚úÖ Valid

üìä Execution Flow (Layered Validation):
Input: "test@gmail.com" for email field with format + validator

1. format: email ‚Üí ‚úÖ PASS (valid email format)
2. validator: &validators.check_email_domain(['company.com']) ‚Üí ‚ùå FAIL
   ‚Üí Return: "Email must be from company.com"

Input: "not-an-email" for same field

1. format: email ‚Üí ‚ùå FAIL (invalid email format)
   ‚Üí Return error immediately, plugin validator NEVER runs (fail-fast)

‚úÖ Benefits (The zCLI Way):
  ‚Ä¢ ‚úÖ Consistent Syntax: Same &plugin.function() as zFunc/zDispatch
  ‚Ä¢ ‚úÖ Reuses Infrastructure: Plugin cache, resolve_plugin_invocation, auto-injection
  ‚Ä¢ ‚úÖ Declarative: Business rules in YAML, not Python decorators
  ‚Ä¢ ‚úÖ Layered Validation: Structural ‚Üí Business logic (clear separation)
  ‚Ä¢ ‚úÖ Fail-Fast: Skip expensive plugin logic if basic format invalid
  ‚Ä¢ ‚úÖ Auto-Wired: Works with Week 5.2 zDialog auto-validation automatically!
  ‚Ä¢ ‚úÖ Testable: Validators are pure functions (easy unit tests)
  ‚Ä¢ ‚úÖ Reusable: Same validator across multiple schemas
  ‚Ä¢ ‚úÖ Graceful Degradation: Missing plugin = log warning + skip (no crash)

üéØ Use Cases (When to Use Each):
  ‚Ä¢ Built-in Validators: "Is this an email?" (format: email)
  ‚Ä¢ Plugin Validators: "Is this from approved domain?" (&validators.check_domain)
  ‚Ä¢ Both (Recommended): Structural + business logic (layered validation)

‚úÖ Tests to Add (20+ comprehensive tests):
  ‚Ä¢ Plugin validator execution (valid/invalid)
  ‚Ä¢ Chaining (built-in ‚Üí plugin, fail-fast)
  ‚Ä¢ Plugin not found (graceful skip)
  ‚Ä¢ Plugin exception handling
  ‚Ä¢ Context injection (table, full_data)
  ‚Ä¢ Integration with zDialog auto-validation
  ‚Ä¢ Multiple validators (email domain, username blacklist, SKU uniqueness)

Week 6.1.1: üîó Integrate zExceptions with zTraceback (Industry-Grade Auto-Registration)
üéØ GOAL: Connect Week 4.3 zExceptions with existing zTraceback for automatic interactive error handling

‚ùå CURRENT STATE (Gap Identified):
  ‚Ä¢ zExceptions have actionable hints + context storage
  ‚Ä¢ zTraceback has interactive handler + exception history
  ‚Ä¢ BUT: They don't talk to each other!
  ‚Ä¢ Result: Exceptions are NOT captured for interactive handling

‚úÖ DESIRED STATE (After 6.1.1):
  ‚Ä¢ All zCLIException instances auto-register with zTraceback (zero boilerplate!)
  ‚Ä¢ Enhanced interactive traceback displays .hint attribute
  ‚Ä¢ Exception history tracking works across all subsystems automatically
  ‚Ä¢ Optional smart recovery actions for common errors (future enhancement)

üèÜ CHOSEN STRATEGY: Option B - Auto-Registration (Industry-Grade)
  ‚Ä¢ Why: Matches Django/Flask/FastAPI patterns (thread-local context)
  ‚Ä¢ Why: Zero boilerplate (forget-proof, automatic everywhere)
  ‚Ä¢ Why: Thread-safe + async-safe (production-ready)
  ‚Ä¢ Why: 90% push to industry-grade zolo-zcli architecture
  ‚Ä¢ Bonus: Keep ExceptionContext as power-user feature for explicit control

üìã Implementation Tasks (5 steps):

1. ‚úÖ Add Thread-Local Context to zCLI (Foundation):
  ‚Ä¢ Add contextvars.ContextVar('current_zcli') to zCLI.py
  ‚Ä¢ Register instance in zCLI.__init__() with _current_zcli.set(self)
  ‚Ä¢ Add get_current_zcli() helper function
  ‚Ä¢ Add __enter__/__exit__ context manager support
  ‚Ä¢ Thread-safe, async-safe (follows Django/Flask pattern)

2. ‚úÖ Modify zCLIException Base Class (Auto-Register):
  ‚Ä¢ Add _register_with_traceback() method to base class
  ‚Ä¢ Call from __init__() to auto-log all exceptions
  ‚Ä¢ Use get_current_zcli() to access zTraceback
  ‚Ä¢ Fail silently if no zCLI context (don't break exception raising)
  ‚Ä¢ Pass .hint and .context to zTraceback.log_exception()

3. ‚úÖ Enhance display_formatted_traceback() (Show Hints):
  ‚Ä¢ Check hasattr(exc, 'hint') and display with zDisplay
  ‚Ä¢ Show exception-specific context (exc.context)
  ‚Ä¢ Use Week 4.3 actionable format (field + constraint + hint)
  ‚Ä¢ Dual-mode: Terminal inline errors + zBifrost WebSocket events

4. ‚úÖ Add ExceptionContext as Power-User Feature (Optional):
  ‚Ä¢ Keep existing ExceptionContext for explicit control
  ‚Ä¢ Use for retry operations or custom context
  ‚Ä¢ Works alongside auto-registration (best of both worlds)

5. ‚úÖ Comprehensive Tests + Documentation:
  ‚Ä¢ Test auto-registration works (raise exception ‚Üí appears in history)
  ‚Ä¢ Test thread safety (multiple zCLI instances)
  ‚Ä¢ Test .hint display in interactive menu
  ‚Ä¢ Test context preservation (exc.context available)

  ‚Ä¢ üî¥ Magic Strings: 30+ found (logging, session keys, zSpark keys, env vars, defaults)
  ‚Ä¢ üî¥ DRY Violations: 3 major patterns (logging prefix 5x, zSpark dict check 4x, nested dict structure)
  ‚Ä¢ ‚ö†Ô∏è Docstring Issues: 3 verbose/vague docstrings
  ‚Ä¢ ‚úÖ zPaths Dependency: N/A (architecturally correct - session is runtime state, not file-based)

  ‚Ä¢ Subsystem Name: "SessionConfig" (lines 30, 42)

Week 6.2.9: üîç Audit & Refactor config_validator.py (Naming Convention + Magic Strings) ‚úÖ COMPLETE
üéØ GOAL: Audit config_validator.py (286 lines) - determine if redundant, fix naming convention, eliminate magic strings

‚ö†Ô∏è WHY THIS MATTERS:
  ‚Ä¢ üî• Redundancy Question: User asked: "Isn't validation in zData/zDialog and error handling in utils?"
  ‚Ä¢ üî• Architectural Clarity: ConfigValidator is a ONE-TIME utility (validates at startup, then discarded)
  ‚Ä¢ üî• Naming Inconsistency: File is config_validator.py but it's NOT a state-holding config module
  ‚Ä¢ üî• Pattern Violation: config_*.py pattern should be for persistent modules only

üîç COMPREHENSIVE AUDIT FINDINGS:

1. ‚ùì Is ConfigValidator Redundant?
  ‚Ä¢ Answer: NO - It serves a distinct purpose!
  ‚Ä¢ Comparison Table:
    - zData/DataValidator: Validates data against schemas (runtime, data operations)
    - zDialog AutoValidation: Validates form inputs (user interaction)
    - ConfigValidator: Validates zSpark_obj config (startup only, fail-fast)
  ‚Ä¢ What ConfigValidator Does:
    1. ‚úÖ Validates zWorkspace path exists and is a directory
    2. ‚úÖ Validates zMode is "Terminal" or "zBifrost"
    3. ‚úÖ Validates WebSocket config (port range 1-65535, host format)
    4. ‚úÖ Validates HTTP server config (port range, serve_path exists)
    5. ‚úÖ PORT CONFLICT DETECTION: Ensures websocket & http_server don't use same port!
  ‚Ä¢ Without it: Bad config causes cryptic errors deep in subsystem initialization
  ‚Ä¢ With it: Clear error messages at startup with actionable fixes
  ‚Ä¢ Usage: Used in EXACTLY ONE PLACE - zConfig.py lines 68-70
  ‚Ä¢ Test Coverage: 18 unit tests + 4 integration tests = 22 tests validating its functionality
  ‚Ä¢ Verdict: ‚úÖ NOT redundant - provides critical fail-fast validation

2. üî¥ NAMING & ARCHITECTURAL INCONSISTENCY (CRITICAL):
  ‚Ä¢ File Name: config_validator.py ‚ùå Breaks config_*.py pattern
  ‚Ä¢ Pattern Analysis:
    - ‚úÖ config_paths.py - State module (persistent instance)
    - ‚úÖ config_machine.py - State module (persistent instance)
    - ‚úÖ config_session.py - State module (persistent instance)
    - ‚úÖ config_logger.py - State module (persistent instance)
    - ‚úÖ config_websocket.py - State module (persistent instance)
    - ‚úÖ config_http_server.py - State module (persistent instance)
    - ‚ùå config_validator.py - ONE-TIME UTILITY (validates once, then discarded!)
  ‚Ä¢ Architectural Problem:
    - All config_*.py files hold persistent state (attributes accessed throughout runtime)
    - ConfigValidator is instantiated, calls .validate() once, then discarded
    - It's a HELPER UTILITY, not a configuration module!
  ‚Ä¢ Impact: Misleading name suggests it's a persistent config module when it's not

3. üî¥ Magic Strings (20+ occurrences):
  ‚Ä¢ Logging Prefix: "[CONFIG VALIDATION]" (multiple occurrences)
    - Solution: LOG_PREFIX = "[CONFIG VALIDATION]"
  ‚Ä¢ Valid Modes (2x): ["Terminal", "zBifrost"] (line 37)
    - Solution: Already has VALID_MODES constant ‚úÖ (but could be class constant)
  ‚Ä¢ Config Keys (10+ occurrences):
    - "zWorkspace", "zMode", "websocket", "http_server"
    - "port", "host", "serve_path", "enabled"
    - "require_auth", "allowed_origins"
    - Solution: Module-level constants for all config keys
  ‚Ä¢ Error Messages (10+ occurrences):
    - Hardcoded error messages with format strings
    - Solution: Error message templates as constants
  ‚Ä¢ Port Range (2x): 1, 65535 (port validation)
    - Solution: PORT_MIN = 1, PORT_MAX = 65535

Week 6.3.6.6: üîê Three-Tier Authentication Architecture + Multi-User Support
üìÅ Files: config_session.py, zAuth/, bridge_auth.py
üìä Complexity: HIGH (architectural redesign + multi-app support)
‚è∞ Effort: 2-3 days (implementation) + 0.5 day (validation of Scenario A)

üèóÔ∏è ARCHITECTURAL VISION: Three-Tier Authentication + Multi-User Support

üéØ THREE AUTHENTICATION LAYERS:

Layer 1: zSession Auth (zCLI/Zolo Users)
  ‚Ä¢ Internal zCLI users authenticated via session["zAuth"]["zSession"]
  ‚Ä¢ Enables Zolo cloud features, premium plugins, analytics
  ‚Ä¢ No token required for internal connections (session-based)
  ‚Ä¢ Example: Developer using zcli load users.yaml

Layer 2: Application Auth (End Users)
  ‚Ä¢ External users of applications BUILT on zCLI
  ‚Ä¢ Configurable user model (developer defines schema: zSchema.store_users.yaml)
  ‚Ä¢ Token-based validation against app's user database
  ‚Ä¢ Example: Customer shopping at "Alice's Store" (has NO zCLI account)

Layer 3: Dual-Auth (Both Contexts)
  ‚Ä¢ BOTH zSession AND application auth active simultaneously
  ‚Ä¢ Enables zCLI features + app-specific permissions
  ‚Ä¢ Example: Store owner using zCLI analytics plugin on their store

üö® Current Gap: Only Layer 1 partially implemented (hardcoded user model).
üéØ Goal: Full three-tier architecture with configurable auth providers.

üîÑ TWO MULTI-USER SCENARIOS (BOTH REQUIRED):

Scenario A: Multiple Concurrent Users on zServer (SERVER-SIDE)
  ‚Ä¢ ‚úÖ Already Supported by Bifrost!
  ‚Ä¢ eCommerce store with 100 customers shopping simultaneously
  ‚Ä¢ Each WebSocket connection = independent authentication
  ‚Ä¢ Alice ‚Üí customer_alice, Bob ‚Üí customer_bob, Charlie ‚Üí customer_charlie
  ‚Ä¢ Handled by self.authenticated_clients = {} dict in bridge_auth.py
  ‚Ä¢ No code changes needed - validate in tests!

Scenario B: One User, Multiple App Authentications (CLIENT-SIDE)
  ‚Ä¢ üöß Week 6.3.6.6 implements this!
  ‚Ä¢ Store owner (Alice) uses ONE zCLI instance
  ‚Ä¢ Opens Store tab ‚Üí logged in as customer_alice
  ‚Ä¢ Opens Admin tab ‚Üí logged in as owner_alice
  ‚Ä¢ Opens Analytics tab ‚Üí logged in as analyst_alice
  ‚Ä¢ All 3 identities persist in session["zAuth"]["applications"] dict
  ‚Ä¢ active_app tracks which app is currently focused

Real-World Example (Both Combined):
  ‚Ä¢ zServer handles 100 concurrent customers (Scenario A ‚úÖ)
  ‚Ä¢ Store owner has 3 simultaneous app logins (Scenario B üöß)
  ‚Ä¢ Total: 100 server connections + owner's multi-app session

üìã SUB-TASKS:

See detailed implementation plans in sub-tasks 6.3.6.6a through 6.3.6.6d below.
Week 6.3.6 Architectural Auth 2-3 days
Week 6.3.6.6a: üîß Session Structure Redesign (config_session.py) - NEEDS REVISION
üìÅ File: zConfig/zConfig_modules/config_session.py
üìä Complexity: HIGH (breaking change to session dict)
‚è∞ Effort: 0.5-1 day (initial) + 0.1 day (multi-app revision)

‚ö†Ô∏è CURRENT STATUS: PARTIALLY COMPLETE

‚úÖ What's Implemented:
  ‚Ä¢ Three-tier nested structure (zSession, application, active_context)
  ‚Ä¢ 9 new constants added and exported
  ‚Ä¢ zAuth module updated (login, logout, status, etc.)
  ‚Ä¢ All tests passing (36 tests, zConfig suite)

‚ö†Ô∏è What's MISSING (Multi-App Support):
  ‚Ä¢ Current: "application" (singular) - single app only
  ‚Ä¢ Target: "applications" (plural) - multi-app dict
  ‚Ä¢ Missing: "active_app" field to track focused app
  ‚Ä¢ Need: Empty dict instead of populated single app structure

üéØ GOAL: Restructure session["zAuth"] to support three authentication contexts + multi-app support (Scenario B)

üîç OLD Structure (Flat - Pre-6.3.6.6a):

session["zAuth"] = {
  "id": 123,
  "username": "alice@company.com",
  "role": "pro",
  "API_Key": "zcli_token_xyz"
}

‚úÖ CURRENT Structure (Three-Tier, SINGLE-APP - Implemented):

session["zAuth"] = {
  "zSession": {
    "authenticated": False,
    "id": None,
    "username": None,
    "role": None,
    "api_key": None
  },
  "application": { # ‚ö†Ô∏è SINGULAR - only ONE app!
    "authenticated": False,
    "id": None,
    "username": None,
    "role": None,
    "api_key": None,
    "context": None # Which application? (confusing!)
  },
  "active_context": None, # "zSession", "application", or "dual"
  "dual_mode": False
}

üéØ TARGET Structure (Three-Tier + MULTI-APP - Needed for Scenario B):

session["zAuth"] = {
  "zSession": {
    "authenticated": False,
    "id": None,
    "username": None,
    "role": None,
    "api_key": None
  },
  "applications": { # ‚úÖ PLURAL - Dict of multiple apps!
    "ecommerce_store": {
      "authenticated": True,
      "id": 456,
      "username": "customer_bob",
      "role": "customer",
      "api_key": "store_token_xyz"
    },
    "analytics_dashboard": {
      "authenticated": True,
      "id": 789,
      "username": "analyst_alice",
      "role": "analyst",
      "api_key": "analytics_token_abc"
    }
  },
  "active_app": None, # ‚úÖ NEW - Which app is currently focused?
  "active_context": None, # "zSession", "application", or "dual"
  "dual_mode": False
}

üîë KEY DIFFERENCES (Current vs. Target):

Aspect Current (Single-App) Target (Multi-App)
Constant Name ZAUTH_KEY_APPLICATION ZAUTH_KEY_APPLICATIONS
Structure Type Single dict with user data Dict of dicts (keyed by app name)
App Tracking "context": None (inside app) "active_app": None (top-level)
Multiple Apps? ‚ùå No - only one app at a time ‚úÖ Yes - unlimited simultaneous apps
Supports Scenario B? ‚ùå No ‚úÖ Yes


üéØ Multi-App Use Cases:
  ‚Ä¢ User logs into Store A as customer_bob ‚Üí opens Analytics as analyst_alice
  ‚Ä¢ Both authentications persist simultaneously
  ‚Ä¢ Switching between apps doesn't lose authentication
  ‚Ä¢ active_app tracks which app is currently focused

üìã SPECIFIC CHANGES NEEDED (Multi-App Revision):

File 1: config_session.py (Lines 113-124)
- ZAUTH_KEY_APPLICATION = "application"
- ZAUTH_KEY_CONTEXT = "context"
+ ZAUTH_KEY_APPLICATIONS = "applications"
+ ZAUTH_KEY_ACTIVE_APP = "active_app"

File 2: config_session.py (Lines 259-266)
- ZAUTH_KEY_APPLICATION: {
- ZAUTH_KEY_AUTHENTICATED: False,
- ZAUTH_KEY_ID: None,
- ...
- ZAUTH_KEY_CONTEXT: None
- },
+ ZAUTH_KEY_APPLICATIONS: {}, # Empty dict for multi-app
+ ZAUTH_KEY_ACTIVE_APP: None,

File 3: config_session.py (Docstring lines 14-16)
- session["zAuth"]["application"] contains app-specific user credentials
+ session["zAuth"]["applications"] is a dict of app-specific credentials
+ Multiple apps can be authenticated simultaneously

File 4: zConfig_modules/__init__.py (Lines 96-104)
- "ZAUTH_KEY_APPLICATION",
- "ZAUTH_KEY_CONTEXT",
+ "ZAUTH_KEY_APPLICATIONS",
+ "ZAUTH_KEY_ACTIVE_APP",

üìä Impact:
  ‚Ä¢ Lines changed: ~8 lines across 2 files
  ‚Ä¢ Risk: LOW (constants not yet used by any code)
  ‚Ä¢ Tests: Still passing (structure unused until Week 6.3.6.6b)
  ‚Ä¢ Breaking changes: None (single-app constants never used yet)

üö® DECISION REQUIRED: Single-App vs. Multi-App

Option A: Keep Single-App (Status Quo)
  ‚Ä¢ ‚úÖ No additional changes needed
  ‚Ä¢ ‚úÖ Faster to proceed to Week 6.3.6.6b
  ‚Ä¢ ‚ùå Does NOT support Scenario B (multi-app per user)
  ‚Ä¢ ‚ùå User can only be authenticated to ONE app at a time
  ‚Ä¢ ‚ùå Switching apps loses previous authentication
  ‚Ä¢ ‚ö†Ô∏è Would require migration LATER (backward compatibility pain)

Use Case Example:
  ‚Ä¢ Store owner opens "Store" tab ‚Üí authenticated as customer_alice
  ‚Ä¢ Opens "Admin" tab ‚Üí LOSES store authentication, must re-login
  ‚Ä¢ ‚ùå Cannot have both active simultaneously

Option B: Multi-App Architecture (Recommended)
  ‚Ä¢ ‚úÖ Supports Scenario B (unlimited simultaneous apps)
  ‚Ä¢ ‚úÖ Change is TINY right now (8 lines across 2 files)
  ‚Ä¢ ‚úÖ No backward compatibility needed (constants not yet used)
  ‚Ä¢ ‚úÖ Aligns with your explicit vision ("we need both scenarios")
  ‚Ä¢ ‚úÖ Much harder to migrate later (would need backward compat)
  ‚Ä¢ ‚úÖ Tests still pass (structure unused until 6.3.6.6b)
  ‚Ä¢ ‚ö†Ô∏è Adds ~10 minutes of work now

Use Case Example:
  ‚Ä¢ Store owner opens "Store" tab ‚Üí authenticated as customer_alice
  ‚Ä¢ Opens "Admin" tab ‚Üí authenticated as owner_alice
  ‚Ä¢ Opens "Analytics" tab ‚Üí authenticated as analyst_alice
  ‚Ä¢ ‚úÖ All 3 identities persist simultaneously
  ‚Ä¢ ‚úÖ Switch between tabs without re-authentication

üí° RECOMMENDATION: Option B (Multi-App)

Why Option B?
  1. User explicitly requested it: "We need both Scenario A and B"
  2. Change is trivial NOW: 8 lines, 10 minutes, zero risk
  3. Painful to migrate LATER: Would require backward compatibility, data migration, etc.
  4. Aligns with vision: Store owner needs multiple simultaneous logins
  5. No downside: Same complexity for Week 6.3.6.6b either way
  6. We're on clean commit: Easy to revert if needed

The Decision:
  ‚Ä¢ It's literally changing "application" ‚Üí "applications" (add 1 letter!)
  ‚Ä¢ And changing {...populated dict...} ‚Üí {} (empty dict)
  ‚Ä¢ And adding "active_app": None (1 line!)
  ‚Ä¢ Total effort: < 10 minutes. Total value: architectural alignment with vision.

Week 6.3.6.6b: üîê zAuth Module Enhancement (Multi-Context Support)
üìÅ Files: zAuth/zAuth.py, zAuth/zAuth_modules/authentication.py
üìä Complexity: HIGH (core authentication logic)
‚è∞ Effort: 0.5-1 day

üéØ GOAL: Enable zAuth to handle both zSession and application-level authentication

üìã Implementation Tasks:

1. Update authentication.py Login Logic
  ‚Ä¢ Import new session constants from config_session
  ‚Ä¢ Update login() to populate session["zAuth"]["zSession"]
  ‚Ä¢ Set active_context = "zSession" after successful zCLI login
  ‚Ä¢ Add authenticated = True flag in zSession context

2. Add New authenticate_app_user() Method (Multi-App Support)
  ‚Ä¢ Signature: authenticate_app_user(self, app_name: str, token: str, config: dict) -> dict
  ‚Ä¢ Parameters:
    - app_name: Application identifier (e.g., "ecommerce_store", "analytics_dashboard")
    - token: API key/token to validate
    - config: Auth config with user model path, field mappings
  ‚Ä¢ Query application user database (configurable model)
  ‚Ä¢ Populate session["zAuth"]["applications"][app_name] on success
  ‚Ä¢ Set active_app = app_name
  ‚Ä¢ Set active_context = "application" (or "dual" if zSession also authenticated)
  ‚Ä¢ Return auth result dict

2b. Add switch_app() Method (NEW!)
  ‚Ä¢ Signature: switch_app(self, app_name: str) -> bool
  ‚Ä¢ Switch focus to a different authenticated application
  ‚Ä¢ Validate that app_name exists in applications dict
  ‚Ä¢ Update active_app = app_name
  ‚Ä¢ Return True if successful, False if app not authenticated

2c. Add get_app_user() Helper (NEW!)
  ‚Ä¢ Signature: get_app_user(self, app_name: str) -> dict
  ‚Ä¢ Retrieve auth info for specific application
  ‚Ä¢ Return session["zAuth"]["applications"][app_name] if exists
  ‚Ä¢ Return None if app not authenticated

3. Add set_active_context() Method
  ‚Ä¢ Signature: set_active_context(self, context: str) -> None
  ‚Ä¢ Valid contexts: "zSession", "application", "dual"
  ‚Ä¢ Update session["zAuth"]["active_context"]
  ‚Ä¢ Update session["zAuth"]["dual_mode"] if context is "dual"
  ‚Ä¢ Validate requested context has authenticated user

4. Add get_active_user() Helper Method (Multi-App Aware)
  ‚Ä¢ Returns user dict for current active context
  ‚Ä¢ If active_context == "zSession": return session["zAuth"]["zSession"]
  ‚Ä¢ If active_context == "application": return session["zAuth"]["applications"][active_app]
  ‚Ä¢ If active_context == "dual": return both zSession + active_app as dict

5. Update logout() Method (Multi-App Support)
  ‚Ä¢ Signature: logout(self, context: str = "zSession", app_name: str = None)
  ‚Ä¢ If context == "zSession": Clear zSession auth
  ‚Ä¢ If context == "application": Clear specific app (requires app_name)
  ‚Ä¢ If context == "all_apps": Clear all applications
  ‚Ä¢ If context == "all": Clear everything (zSession + all apps)
  ‚Ä¢ Update active_context and active_app appropriately

6. Add Application Auth Configuration Support
  ‚Ä¢ Define config schema for application authentication:
    {
      "user_model": "@.store_users.users",
      "id_field": "id",
      "username_field": "email",
      "role_field": "role",
      "api_key_field": "api_key"
    }
  ‚Ä¢ Load from zConfig or method parameter
  ‚Ä¢ Validate config structure before using

7. Update Docstrings
  ‚Ä¢ Document three-tier architecture in module docstring
  ‚Ä¢ Add examples for each authentication scenario
  ‚Ä¢ Document configuration schema for application auth

‚úÖ Validation:
  ‚Ä¢ zCLI login populates zSession context correctly
  ‚Ä¢ authenticate_app_user() works with custom user models
  ‚Ä¢ Context switching works correctly
  ‚Ä¢ Logout clears appropriate contexts
  ‚Ä¢ Existing zAuth tests still pass
Week 6.3.6.6 zAuth Core Logic 0.5-1 day
Week 6.3.6.6c: üîê bridge_auth.py Three-Tier Implementation
üìÅ File: bifrost/bridge_modules/bridge_auth.py (199 lines)
üìä Complexity: HIGH (industry-grade + three-tier logic)
‚è∞ Effort: 1 day

üéØ GOAL: Refactor to industry-grade AND implement three-tier authentication

üìã Implementation Tasks:

Phase 1: Industry-Grade Foundation
  ‚Ä¢ Add path comment
  ‚Ä¢ Add 70+ module-level constants (log prefix, close codes, auth keys, etc.)
  ‚Ä¢ Add 100% type hints to all 8 methods
  ‚Ä¢ Add input validation (logger, allowed_origins IndexError, query parsing)
  ‚Ä¢ Extract DRY helpers: _get_ws_headers(), _get_ws_path()
  ‚Ä¢ Replace broad except Exception with specific exceptions
  ‚Ä¢ Enhance all docstrings (module, class, methods) with three-tier architecture notes

Phase 2: Three-Tier Authentication Logic
  ‚Ä¢ Import new session constants from config_session

    Step 1: Check zSession (Internal zCLI Connections)
      ‚Ä¢ If walker.zcli.session["zAuth"]["zSession"]["authenticated"]:
        - Return zSession user (no token required)
        - Log: "Internal zCLI connection authenticated via session"
        - Return dict with context = "zSession"

    Step 2: Check Application Auth (External Users)
      ‚Ä¢ Extract token from query params or headers
      ‚Ä¢ If token present:
        - Call walker.zcli.auth.authenticate_app_user(token, auth_config)
        - If success: return application user with context = "application"
      ‚Ä¢ If no token and require_auth: close connection

    Step 3: Dual-Auth Detection (Advanced)
      ‚Ä¢ If BOTH zSession AND token present:
        - Authenticate both contexts
        - Set dual_mode = True
        - Return dict with both users and context = "dual"

  Issue: generate_cache_key() doesn't include user/app context
  Risk: User A's query results cached, User B gets same cache key ‚Üí data leak!

    ‚Ä¢ Cache key: md5("users|read|...")
    ‚Ä¢ Bob (user) queries same ‚Üí gets Alice's admin results! üî•
  Fix Required: Include user_id + app_name + role in cache key

  Example:
    ‚Ä¢ "ecommerce_store" queries: SELECT * FROM orders
    ‚Ä¢ "analytics_dashboard" queries same table ‚Üí gets ecommerce orders! üî•

üéØ TARGET USE CASES:
1Ô∏è‚É£ Users building apps that integrate with Google, Spotify, Instagram APIs
2Ô∏è‚É£ "Sign in with Google/Facebook" for zCLI applications
3Ô∏è‚É£ Enterprise SSO via OAuth 2.0/OpenID Connect

üéØ GOAL: Enable zAuth to authenticate via third-party OAuth providers

üìã Proposed Implementation:

1. Add OAuth Provider Module
  ‚Ä¢ Create zAuth/zAuth_modules/oauth_provider.py
  ‚Ä¢ Support OAuth 2.0 flows: authorization code, implicit, client credentials
  ‚Ä¢ Support OpenID Connect (identity layer on OAuth 2.0)
  ‚Ä¢ Built-in providers: Google, Facebook, GitHub, Spotify, Instagram, Twitter
  ‚Ä¢ Custom provider support (configurable endpoints)

2. OAuth Methods
  ‚Ä¢ get_authorization_url(provider, scopes) -> str: Generate OAuth URL
  ‚Ä¢ exchange_code_for_token(provider, code) -> dict: Exchange code for access token
  ‚Ä¢ get_user_info(provider, access_token) -> dict: Fetch user profile
  ‚Ä¢ refresh_token(provider, refresh_token) -> dict: Refresh expired token
  ‚Ä¢ revoke_token(provider, token) -> bool: Revoke access

3. Session Structure Enhancement
  ‚Ä¢ Add OAuth fields to application auth:
    "auth_method": "oauth" (vs "token" or "password")
    "oauth_provider": "google" (provider name)
    "access_token": "ya29.a0AfH6..." (OAuth access token)
    "refresh_token": "1//0gH..." (OAuth refresh token)
    "token_expires_at": "2025-10-30T12:00:00Z" (expiry timestamp)
    "scopes": ["email", "profile"] (granted scopes)

4. Provider Configuration
  ‚Ä¢ Load from zConfig or environment variables:
    ZOLO_OAUTH_GOOGLE_CLIENT_ID
    ZOLO_OAUTH_GOOGLE_CLIENT_SECRET
    ZOLO_OAUTH_GOOGLE_REDIRECT_URI
  ‚Ä¢ Support multiple providers simultaneously
  ‚Ä¢ Validate config on provider initialization

5. Bifrost Integration
  ‚Ä¢ Add OAuth callback handler in bridge_auth.py
  ‚Ä¢ Support OAuth redirect flow via WebSocket
  ‚Ä¢ Handle OAuth errors and user cancellations
  ‚Ä¢ Display OAuth consent screen in GUI mode

6. Dependencies
  ‚Ä¢ Add authlib>=1.3.0 to pyproject.toml
  ‚Ä¢ Or use requests-oauthlib for simpler implementation
  ‚Ä¢ Add cryptography for JWT token validation (OpenID Connect)

7. Testing
  ‚Ä¢ Mock OAuth provider responses
  ‚Ä¢ Test token refresh logic
  ‚Ä¢ Test token expiry handling
  ‚Ä¢ Test each provider's quirks (Google, Facebook, etc.)

8. Documentation
  ‚Ä¢ Update zAuth_GUIDE.md with OAuth examples
  ‚Ä¢ Create OAuth_SETUP.md for provider configuration
  ‚Ä¢ Add code examples for each provider
